At around 7:00 AM yesterday morning, seven robbers suddenly broke into the Jiaji Foreign Grocery Store at No. 9, Lane 3, Ruyi Lane, Laotaiping Street, Nanshi. They held three handguns and warned everyone not to make a sound. They drove everyone to a corner and assigned accomplices to watch over them. They then began to search and rob the store, taking more than 2,000 yuan in cash. They also robbed two customers, including Mr. Lu, of more than 400 yuan in cash. Not satisfied, they broke into the residence of a tenant surnamed Wu and robbed him of 300 yuan in cash, totaling more than 1,000 yuan in losses. After looting, the robbers gave a secret signal and fled with the stolen goods. When the 16th Precinct learned of the incident, they dispatched police officers to surround and capture the robbers, but they had already fled far away. They only recorded the appearance and clothing of the robbers for future reference. Patrol Captain Dong Mingde of the Detective Team was assigned to investigate the store to facilitate the arrest of the fleeing robbers and bring them to justice for interrogation.

Man Collecting Paper Ingots and Ashes Dies from Vomiting Blood on the Road 138

At 7:20 AM yesterday morning, a man surnamed Jia, approximately 30 years old and a native of Shaoxing, who made a living collecting paper ingots and ashes, was carrying a bamboo basket of ashes on his shoulder, collecting ashes when he walked into Wenyuanfang, No. 10, Pishenai Road, French Concession. Suddenly, he vomited fresh blood, which poured out like a tide. He immediately fell to the ground and died. The Chinese constable from Nos. 679 reported this to the Zhafei Police Department, who dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Crematory to await identification of his family. The court will be requested to send personnel for inspection today.

Woman Runs Away with Paramour Behind Her Husband’s Back 139

Ji Jinkui, 31 years old, a native of Yancheng, resides on Zhongshan Road, Shanghai. He married a woman named Chen, 24 years old, who is quite beautiful. Recently, she became acquainted with Zhang Fulin, a fellow villager, and eloped with him last month without her husband's knowledge. Ji Jinkui found out that she was hiding with Zhang on Robert Street yesterday. He reported this to the local police station, who arrested Ji Chen and Zhang Fulin and transferred them to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The bureau, considering the case involved enticement and elopement, prepared a document and sent them to the General Bureau for further investigation.

Yan Jinbiao Case Sent Back for Retrial 140

Around 6:00 PM on August 15th, 1931, a case of robbers killing their own kind occurred in Room 2 of the Fashang Hotel on Xixinqiao Street, French Concession. Jiang Zhonghan, Xia Yongsheng, and a man surnamed Xue, all from Jiangbei, were killed, and Zhong Ziqing was injured. Afterwards, the French police arrested Yan Jinbiao, a native of Funing, as the murderer and sent him to the court. He was sentenced to death after three trials and appeals, and the final judgment was confirmed. On April 6th, 1934, Yan was executed according to law. During the trial, Yan confessed that the mastermind was Li Guocheng, also known as Chen Youliang. Later, Yan's wife arrested Li in the Rihui Port area of Nanshi, and the Shanghai Public Security Bureau reported this to the Second Special Court for retrieval and handed it over to the Legal Police Affairs Department for investigation and prosecution. At the end of the trial, Li was sentenced to death. He appealed to the Higher Third Branch Court, but the result was a rejection. Li still refused to accept this and appealed to the Supreme Court to overturn the original judgment. The Supreme Court reviewed the entire case file and found that the facts of the case were still unclear. Therefore, the retrial judgment was again overturned and sent back to the Higher Third Branch Court for another retrial. The Higher Third Branch Court, upon receiving the order, assigned Judge Wang Yue to handle the case. The wife of Yan Jinbiao was ordered to appear for an investigation hearing the day before yesterday. As a result, Yan's wife could not be found to summon, so she did not appear, and no hearing was held to question Li.

Arrest for Selling Drugs at the Entrance of Sanguantang Alley; Drugs Came from a Korean Woman; Two Chinese Offenders Sentenced to Seven Years Each 141

Sanguantang Alley on Huaji Road is a major base for selling and consuming the drug heroin. Wang Ruilin, a Chinese detective of the Huishan Police Department, learned at 10:20 AM the day before yesterday that two men from Ningbo, Wang Zixiang, and Chen Haiqing from Hubei, were selling this drug at the entrance of the alley. He sent someone to buy it, which was confirmed to be true. He then coordinated with a Western detective to rush to the location and arrest Wang and Chen. Fourteen small packets of heroin were found on Wang. After questioning, it was learned that Chen introduced Wang to get the drugs from a Korean woman at No. 11 Xian Road. He would get forty packets of drugs every day, selling each packet for 24 copper coins. The detectives then cooperated with Japanese police to arrest the Korean woman at that address and send her to the Japanese Consulate for handling. Wang and Chen were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District yesterday. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, detailed the case and requested prosecution. Detective Wang then reported the entire incident. The drugs were presented for inspection. Judge Zhong Qing questioned the two defendants, who confessed clearly. Wang Zixiang and Chen Haiqing were each sentenced to seven years in prison, and the heroin was confiscated.

Paramour Declares Separation; Paramour Holds Grudge and Commits Assault; Gu Shutian Interrogated and Sentenced 142

Lin Xiaomei, a 23-year-old woman from Ningbo, lives at No. 20, Lane 405, Dongxi Huade Road. She recently became involved with Gu Shutian, a local resident, for several months. Because Lin had to return to Ningbo, and Gu was unable to support her lifestyle, she declared that she was severing their relationship. This caused Gu to hold a grudge and seek revenge. On the 19th of the month, at 8:00 AM, Gu learned that Lin had returned to Shanghai. He took a skinning knife and went to Lin’s residence. Taking her by surprise, he stabbed her twice in the right hip and then fled. Lin reported this to the police station, and Lin's injuries were quite serious and have not yet healed. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, at 8:30 PM, Gu sent a person named Yang Hongsheng to Lin's place to mediate. This was reported to the Hongkou Police Department, and Chinese detective Liu Zhaonian was ordered to detain Yang for questioning. Only then did he learn that Gu was hiding in Chenjia Alley, Hongzhen. They then cooperated with the Public Security Bureau to arrest Gu. Yesterday, he was escorted to the Fifth Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted him for the crime of injury under Article 277, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Lin Xiaomei declared that she wanted him to be severely prosecuted. Gu Huatian confessed to the assault. Judge Ye Shengchao, after reviewing the confession, announced in court that Gu Shutian was sentenced to 40 days of detention, and the knife was confiscated.

Villagers Fight Over Shadow Puppet Show; Turns into Bloody Tragedy 143

Zhu Adi, the current village head of Xiaoji Genglang, Qibao Town, West Shanghai, joined with villagers to initiate a shadow puppet show the night before last. Ma Boyu and others, the son of Ma Rusheng, the owner of the Ma Family Oil Workshop who lived nearby, argued over the shadow puppet show. That night, both sides gathered more than a hundred hooligans each, armed with clubs, axes, and other weapons. A disagreement led to a mutual brawl. As a result, Ma Boyu's right hand was chopped off, including his shoulder and back. Ma Youdi (carpenter), 32 years old, and Ma Agen (tailor, 26 years old), were all cut on their head, face, hands, and feet. The injuries of these three were the most serious, and they are currently in the hospital for treatment. More than ten other people, including Li Jintang, suffered minor injuries. Afterwards, the local police station dispatched a large number of long-gun carrying police officers to the village to arrest people. The murderers had already fled. Village head Zhu Adi and Ma Shenglang, who was performing the show, were taken to the bureau for interrogation.

Young Woman Injured by Paramour with Knife 144

Wang Xiuqin, a 19-year-old local woman, lives in Wangjiazhai, Hongqiao Town, West Shanghai. Xiuqin is very romantic and loves freedom. Last year, she had a relationship with Zhang Jingen, a foreign tailor, and they swore an oath of allegiance. But Wang was fickle and had an affair with a kinsman. Recently, through the introduction of the kinsman, she met someone surnamed Li and was formally engaged last month. The day before yesterday, Wang was passing near the Xujiahui Yaozhujiao Road when Zhang Jingen found out. He took a sharp axe and rushed over to cut Wang on her head, face, and arms. The murderer, seeing that his goal had been achieved, fled. Afterwards, people took Wang by car to the Shanghai Shizhen Hospital on Haige Road for treatment. Fortunately, the injuries were not fatal, and her life was saved.

Fraudulent Collection for Establishing Fertilizer Association; Seven Promoters Arrested; Victims All Testify in Court 146

Wang Yinji, Zhang Bingsheng, Song Keyu, Hao Fengquan, He Wanxuan, Jin Chang, and Shan Xingya, all natives of Yancheng, have recently been defrauding their fellow villagers Hao Huiquan, Zhou Yufan, and Lü Yuxiang, who are boatmen at the docks in the Jiashan Road area, under the guise of establishing the Shanghai Fertilizer Transport Association. They defrauded them of 113 yuan. The case was reported to the Jiayu Road Police Station, which dispatched Chinese detective Chen Jinsheng to cooperate with Western detectives to arrest Wang Yinji and the other six and bring them, along with their records and bylaws, into the police station for detention the day before yesterday. The next morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated the case and requested an extension for detailed investigation. Detective Chen then reported the arrest of the defendants and presented the evidence for inspection. The victims Hao Huiquan, Zhou Yufan, and Lü Yuxiang, testified about being defrauded. When questioned, the defendants stammered and denied soliciting the above-mentioned money, pleading for leniency. Judge Zhong Qing ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation and decision.

Tong Yi Trust Company to Return Part of Deposits; One-Quarter to Be Paid on September 7th 147

After the Tong Yi Trust Company, whose inspectors were appointed by the compensation group, was declared bankrupt by the court, all one-quarter deposits were resolved to be paid out within two weeks at the creditors' meeting on the 15th. The depositors' compensation group of the company held a depositors' meeting at Tianhou Palace at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, with more than 200 people present. Gu Difan chaired the meeting, and Gu Siping took the minutes. The results of the discussion were: (1) The inspector should be selected by the Shanghai depositors, with the selection based on the number of depositor votes and two-thirds of the claims; (2) It was resolved to request that the remaining three-quarters of the deposits and interest be fully repaid within a specified period, based on the Ministry of Finance’s approval; (3) It was resolved to determine the number of inspectors for the savings department as nine; (4) Secret; (5) It was resolved to prevent the company's directors and supervisors from leaving Shanghai without permission, and to request the court to rule; (6) It was resolved that the company's directors and supervisors should not conceal or transfer their property, and to request the court to enforce provisional attachment. According to a report by a reporter from the New Voice News Agency, after the company's bankruptcy liquidator, Li Ding, was ordered by the court to pay depositors one-quarter of their deposits within two weeks, he will liquidate the public bonds deposited in the Central Bank, obtaining 530,000 yuan. The total amount of the company's deposits is 2.4 million yuan, but only over 1 million has been registered. It has been decided that one-quarter will be paid back on September 7th, and the remaining three-quarters will be paid back after the other assets have been liquidated.

Vegetable Vendor Commits Suicide by Cutting Abdomen Due to Severe Stomach Pain 155

Shen Qingyu, a 44-year-old vegetable vendor from Ningbo, lived in a bungalow at No. 13 Baoshan Road, Zhabei. Yesterday morning, while setting up his vegetable stall at the Baoxing Road vegetable market, he suddenly experienced severe abdominal pain and could not sit or stand. — Edited by China Credit

The general overview of Shanghai's industrial and commercial changes in the second quarter of this year is better than that of the first quarter of this year and the same period last year. According to the survey and statistics of this institute, the following table can be listed:

Comparison Table of Various Changes in Shanghai's Industry and Commerce

New Establishments　　Expansions　　Contractions　　Reorganizations　　Closures

Second Quarter of the 24th Year　　20　　11　　462　　116

First Quarter of the 25th Year　　91　　44　　32　　916　　222

Second Quarter of the 25th Year　　111　　51　　29　　714　　181

The number of new establishments and expansions increased in the second quarter compared with the first quarter, while contractions, reorganizations, and closures decreased in the second quarter compared with the first quarter, which sufficiently proves the gradual improvement of the social economy. As for the three months of the second quarter of this year, new establishments in June were slightly less than in the previous two months due to seasonal factors, while closures increased. Statistical Table of Shanghai's Industrial and Commercial Changes by Industry in the Second Quarter of This Year

Shunji Wins Mayor's Cup, Defeating Zhonghua 2-1 159

The citywide Mayor's Cup youth football competition began during the Spring Festival this year, with a total of more than 100 matches. The final was held yesterday afternoon at the city stadium. All ticket revenue was used to purchase a machine for birthday celebrations. The audience was very enthusiastic yesterday. Shunji defeated Zhonghua 2-1 to win the first Mayor's Cup. In addition, there were two exhibition matches. Feixiong defeated Fahua 6-2, and Lianghua defeated Shiguang 2-0. Details are as follows:

Children's Performance

The opening ceremony at 3:00 PM was a children's exhibition match between Feixiong and Fahua. Because Mayor Wu went to Lushan and has not yet returned to Shanghai, Wang Fudan, the acting director of the city stadium, was invited to kick off the match. At that time, the sound of firecrackers rose into the sky. The young athletes on both sides were small and exquisite, and the game was full of highlights. As a result, Feixiong won the first battle with a score of 6-2.

Adult Performance

At 4:10 PM, Lianghua and Shiguang played an adult exhibition match. Football stars Li Yichen, Wan Xianghua, Xu Wenkui, and Zeng Qiuting all played. Shiguang was a joint team of elites from the city. Although the coordination was not very skilled, the individual skills were top-notch. As a result, they lost to Lianghua by only two goals.

Mayor's Cup Match

Finally, the Mayor's Cup final was announced, and the audience became even more excited. The Zhonghua team was a rising star and had a strong desire to win. Lin Gendu broke the record first. Shunji's Luo Douwen, Zhang Jinhai, and other athletes were not willing to be outdone and launched a large-scale counterattack. Under heavy pressure from Zhonghua, they lost two goals in succession. After the time was reported, Shunji won the Mayor's Cup with a score of 2-1.

Mayor's Cup Champion Shunji Team

Awards Ceremony

After the completion of each match, the Small Football Association invited Zhang Binghui, the section chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, to represent the mayor to present the awards. Feixiong won a silver cup from Commander Yang Xiaotian, Fahua won a silver shield from Director Xu Peihuang, Lianghua received a silver shield from Director Pan Gongzhan, Shiguang was given a silver shield from Director Wu Xingya, and Shunji won the Mayor's Cup champion. After the awards were presented, speeches were given and the event ended.

Middle Bar Rematch Final

The middle bar rematch was held at 3:00 PM, divided into two groups, with six people in each group. The top three participants were selected to participate in the final. In the first group, the world record holder, American athlete Harding, and the Far East record holder, Filipino athlete Whyte, competed fiercely. At the last bar, they were only half a step apart. Harding sprinted faster and won the first place by one and a half meters. German athlete Gulden had a good speed in the first five bars, posing a threat to Harding, but his stamina was insufficient and he was eventually eliminated. The third and fourth runners arrived at the finish line at the same time. The referee could not determine the ranking for a while. After the photo was developed, the decision was made. One person was able to participate in the final, while the other failed. There were both lucky and unfortunate people. In the first group, American athlete Patterson won extremely easily, reaching the finish line one meter ahead. The second and third places were very close. The results of the two groups are as follows:

(The following three were eliminated)

At 5:30 PM in the final, Harding was on the outermost lane, followed by Mantikass, Whyte, Magalhaes, and Laurin. Patterson was on the innermost lane. In the first two bars, all six people started and landed at the same time. After that, Harding gradually gained an advantage. After turning into the straight line at the third turn, Harding was one meter ahead. Whyte followed closely, and Laurin was also sprinting desperately behind. By the time they reached the finish line, Harding still maintained a distance of one meter and won the first place. Laurin defeated Whyte by one shoulder. Patterson, who had the best result in the rematch, fell back to fourth place. The other two were ten meters behind. Harding's result was 52.4 seconds, which was much lower than his world record of 50.6 seconds set in 1934 and his Olympic record of 52 seconds set in 1932.

800-Meter Final

The 800-meter final was held at 4:45 PM. Eight people qualified for the final. Two people had to be eliminated, so the competition was extremely fierce. When the gun was fired, Italian athlete Lanci false started. This was a rare phenomenon in track and field races. The race restarted. Canadian black Edwards took the lead and led the crowd. American black Woodlerov was in fourth place, following leisurely. In the first lap, sixteen flying legs advanced side by side, chasing closely. At 600 meters, Woodlerov enlarged his steps, relaxed as usual, and jumped to replace Edwards in the front. Edwards was unwilling to give in and once again bravely strived to be the first. It was just a flash in the pan. Woodlerov went out again at 700 meters and accelerated, sprinting desperately. At the same time, Italian athlete Lanci was also stepping forward behind. Although Edwards gritted his teeth and fought bravely, he was exhausted. As a result, Woodlerov won first place by three meters. The result was 1 minute 52.9 seconds, which was not outstanding. The second, third, and fourth places were one step apart. The United Kingdom was in a downturn, and McCabber and Bakerhouse of Hampshire were eliminated. (The world record and the Olympic record are both held by Hampson of the United Kingdom at 1 minute 49.7 seconds.)

Pole Vault Sino-American-Japanese War

The pole vault final became a confrontation between the American and Japanese athletes, a major battle, which was one of the most exciting scenes in the five days of the Games. Although they fought at night, the order of the top five was not decided until 9:05 PM. However, the spectators who cheered and cheered watched the game with great interest. The trial was held at 10:30 AM, with a total of 35 participants. It was stipulated that they must jump over 3.80 meters to participate in the final in the afternoon. The trial was divided into four groups, starting at 3.50 meters. A total of 25 people jumped over 3.80 meters. Chinese athlete Fu Baolu failed in the first jump at 3.80 meters. It was almost noon. Suddenly, dark clouds gathered, and there was a heavy rain, so it was stopped for 20 minutes. After the rain stopped, Fu jumped over lightly and freely, which was the only one in the Chinese track and field team to win the right to the final. The final began at 4:00 PM, starting at 3.60 meters. French athlete Klibin failed in three jumps and was the first to step down. When it was increased to 3.80 meters, Chilean athlete Sohlegel also retired. When it was increased to 4 meters, 16 people jumped over. An Kui Tao from Japan, who was defeated by Fu Baolu in the last Far East Games, was also among those who jumped over. Fu Baolu was timid and failed three times, so he was eliminated. When it was increased to 4.15 meters, Japanese athletes Nishida Shuhei and Oie Kio, and American athletes Meadows and Gray Reb, all passed on the first jump. Another American athlete, Sefton, passed on the second jump. The other 11 people all completed their merits. The pole vault final became a situation where the United States and three Japanese athletes confronted each other. At this time, the emotions of more than 100,000 spectators were extremely tense. When the Japanese athletes jumped, they all cheered and cheered, especially for Nishida Shuhei, who cheered even more enthusiastically. When the American athletes jumped, they whistled and made strange noises. This phenomenon may be caused by the psychology of helping the weak and eliminating the strong. But no matter whether it was cheering or strange noises, everyone became quiet and silent when they held the pole forward. When it was increased to 4.25 meters, Seton and Nishida both jumped over on the first jump. Meadows, Oie, and Gray Reb all failed to jump over. Among them, it was a pity that Gray Reb's whole body passed the bar very high, but he failed by touching the bar with his hand. On the second jump, when Meadows passed the bar, his left arm touched the bar, but it did not fall off, which was very lucky. Oie followed and jumped over, and the wilting momentum was quite natural. However, Gray Reb, who held the world record (4.37 meters), failed three times and ranked fifth. When it was increased to 4.35 meters, it was already a new record for the Games. (The old record was set by American athlete Miller, the champion of the previous Games. At this time, the twilight was vast, but fortunately the lighting equipment in the venue was excellent, and the lighting after the opening was as bright as day, so it could continue to be held. On the first jump, none of the four people passed. On the second jump, Meadows exerted all his strength and flew in with the pole, passing the bar with a beautiful posture. The whole venue burst into applause and cheers. The other three people all failed to jump three times, so Meadows settled in the top spot. When it was increased to 4.45 meters to try to create a record, Meadows had already jumped over his whole body, but his chest touched the bar when he landed, so he failed, which was a pity. In the next two jumps, he was exhausted and his performance stopped at 4.35 meters. Fu Dun, Oie, and Nishida competed for second place. They first jumped 4.35 meters, but none of them passed. When it was reduced to 4.25 meters, it was still the same. When it was reduced to 4.15 meters, Sefton still failed. Oie and Nishida jumped over one after another. Because they were from the same country, they did not want to compete again, so they tied for second place. This fierce battle did not end until 9:05 PM. Because it was too late for sixth place, they could not jump again, so the 11 people tied for the sixth place.

Education News

Central Implementation: Remedial Education for Out-of-School People (2): Ministry of Education's Radio Broadcasts and Lectures 168

In addition to the above-mentioned counties and cities being required to establish people's schools in various townships in stages, all private schools, organizations, institutions, large factories, farms, stores, and companies in all cities across the country (such as the capital and the locations of provincial and municipal governments) and in areas with developed industry and commerce must establish at least one affiliated people's school to supplement the efforts of the township people's schools where their strength is insufficient.

After the above six-year deadline expires, by July of the Republic of China year 11, a total of 191 million out-of-school people in counties and cities across the country will have received training. The number of people in the people's schools affiliated with various institutions is not included in this calculation. Most out-of-school people under the age of 45 can receive training, and illiteracy can be eliminated throughout the country. B. Phased Provisions for the Number of Trainees: All out-of-school people aged 16 to 45 are the target of education, but because the number is too large to implement simultaneously, two phases should be specified as follows:

(1) Phase 1: That is, from the first year to the fourth year, a total of 86 million people can be trained. Priority should be given to training out-of-school men and women aged 16 to 30.

(2) Phase 2: That is, from the fifth year to the sixth year, all out-of-school men and women under the age of 45 will receive general training.

C. Compulsory Enrollment: In areas where people's schools have been widely established and are sufficient to accommodate the local out-of-school population, all physically healthy out-of-school young people and adult men and women should be ordered by the local organizations in charge of remedial education for out-of-school people to enroll in people's schools according to their age and family situation. Those who should enroll but do not will be given a written warning to their parents, guardians, employers, or themselves, setting a deadline for them to attend school. Those who do not heed the warning may have their names publicly posted as a warning. Those who still do not comply may be fined by the county or city education administrative agency, with the approval of the county government, from one yuan to five yuan, and still be ordered to enroll within a deadline. This fine can be used for the remedial education of out-of-school people in various localities.

D. Regulations on Deferred or Exempted Enrollment: Out-of-school people who have illnesses or other reasons that temporarily prevent them from enrolling may have their parents, guardians, employers, or themselves submit a written request for exemption. Those who have completed short-term primary schools or people's schools are considered to have received remedial education. Those who have received education equivalent to that of people's schools in private schools, families, or factories, companies, or stores, and have passed the examination by the local people's school and been certified, are considered to have received adult remedial education and may be exempted from enrollment.

E. People's Schools Should Be Established Independently in Rural Areas in Principle: The establishment of people's schools in counties and cities should follow the standards of autonomous regions, neighborhoods, townships, and towns. In the first year, one school should be established in a suitable location in each township, and then additional schools should be established year by year. Within the six-year deadline, efforts should be made to ensure that all out-of-school men and women in the entire township receive training to the extent possible. Those that can be established independently should be established independently as much as possible. When it becomes necessary in the future, they can be converted into higher-level people's schools or people's education centers to serve as the central institutions for promoting social education and improving rural areas.

3. Preparations for Implementation

Implementing remedial education for out-of-school people involves a large number of people and requires significant funding. All necessary teachers, school buildings, equipment, etc. must be comprehensively planned and prepared in advance. The matters that need to be prepared are described below:

(A) Training Teachers: According to Article 4 of the Outline of Measures, each county and city should add 20 to 40 schools starting from the 25th year of the Republic. Calculating an average of 30 schools per county, a total of 60,000 schools should be added nationwide in the 2,000 counties and cities. Assuming one principal/teacher per school, 60,000 teachers are needed. Starting from the second year, each county will add 20 schools, and a total of 40,000 schools will need to be added nationwide in the 2,000 counties and cities. Another 40,000 teachers must be added each year. Based on this calculation, 60,000 teachers are needed in the first year, 40,000 more are needed in the second year, totaling 100,000. 140,000 are needed in the third year, 180,000 are needed in the fourth year, 220,000 are needed in the fifth year, and 260,000 are needed in the sixth year. The number of people's schools with two or more classes, teachers other than the principal, and teachers in people's schools affiliated with various institutions and organizations are not included in this calculation. Therefore, the item of teachers must be prepared in advance and trained first in order to be allocated. The education departments of each province should establish teacher training classes for people's education in various regions, recruit students with the equivalent of junior high school graduation level, provide them with two months of training, and, after passing the examination, distribute them to counties and cities to serve as principals or teachers of people's schools. Municipalities directly under the central government should handle this in the location of the municipal government. If the trained teachers are still insufficient for allocation, they may consider appointing civil servants to serve concurrently as teachers of people's schools.

B. Raising Funds: To popularize remedial education for out-of-school people, the funds for running people's schools are to be managed by the municipal government in municipalities directly under the central government. In counties and cities in provinces, the principle is that the provinces and counties should share the burden as appropriate. When the central government has sufficient funds in the future, it may also subsidize them as appropriate. The funds for remedial education for out-of-school people in each province and city should be allocated according to the local situation, either from the provincial and municipal education funds or by designating a certain percentage from the total income of the province and city. The provincial and municipal education departments should prepare a budget each year before the start of the year. The funds for remedial education for out-of-school people in counties and cities should be allocated according to the local situation, either by designating schools or by designating special taxes. People should also be encouraged to donate as much as possible. Each county and city government should include it in the budget each year before the start of the year. (To be continued)

The State of Secondary Education in Jiangxi Province in the 23rd Year of the Republic of China 169

According to a recent survey and statistics on the state of secondary education in Jiangxi Province in the 23rd year of the Republic of China: (1) There are 39 middle schools in the province (11 provincial, 6 county-run, and 22 private). There are a total of 1,380 students (1,139 boys and 241 girls). There are a total of 278 faculty and staff (260 men and 18 women). The total annual expenditure is 211,261 yuan (164,888 yuan for boys' schools and 46,373 yuan for girls' schools). The above three items of middle schools, vocational schools, and normal schools totaled 65 schools, 399 classes, 12,070 students, 1,460 faculty and staff, and an annual expenditure of 1,379,156 yuan in the 23rd year of the Republic of China.

International Amateur Athletic Federation Approves 33 World Records: United States Occupies 20, Owens Alone Accounts for Six; Female Athletes Subject to Examination if Gender Protested

Berlin, August 28 (National Telegram) The International Amateur Athletic Federation has recognized 33 new records in men's track and field, some breaking world records, some equaling world records, and some created at this year's World Games.

Of these 33 new records, 20 belong to American athletes, with Owens alone accounting for six, five of which are new world records and one of which equals a world record.

Owens' five new records are the 220 yards and 200 meters in the 1935 October University Games, each with 20.3 seconds, the 220 yards and 200 meters low hurdles with 22.6 seconds, and the long jump of 26 feet 8 and 1/4 inches (8.13 meters). Other new world records for American athletes are Williams' 400 meters with 46.1 seconds, Towns' 120 yards and 110 meters high hurdles with 14 seconds, Marius' decathlon with 7,900 points, the US team's two-mile relay performance in Berlin's two-mile relay, Froloff's pole vault with 14 feet 6 and a half inches, and Johnson and Albrighton's high jump with 6 feet 9 and 3/4 inches.

The association also recognized the twelve world records set at the World Games. The association also unanimously passed a resolution regarding international women's competitions that, if a formal protest is made regarding a female athlete's gender within two hours after a formal competition, she should immediately be examined by qualified doctors for verification.

Economic Supplement

Re-discussing the Reform of the Currency System in Guangdong Province 176

— Xu Deguang

(1) Key Issues

Regarding the reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province, the author published an article titled "A Humble Suggestion for Reforming the Currency System in Guangdong Province" in this publication last week, advocating: (1) Using the existing silver in Guangdong Province as cash reserves to issue 120 million yuan of new legal tender in the form of silver dollars, with central government bonds allocated as the guarantee reserve; (2) Stipulating a ratio of one silver dollar legal tender to 1.6 yuan of subsidiary notes, and gradually withdrawing 192 million yuan of subsidiary notes with the newly issued legal tender, while issuing Guangdong Financial Treasury Bills to absorb the remaining subsidiary notes as much as possible; (3) Stipulating methods for legal tender to repay debts: all public and private debts incurred before Guangdong Province promulgated the order to centralize silver (the previous article advocated using November 3rd of the 24th year of the Republic (1935) as the dividing line for debts, out of respect for central government laws and regulations, but since the implementation date of legal tender in Guangdong Province was relatively late, the local situation can be considered, taking the date of Guangdong Province's announcement of this order as the standard), all debts should be repaid in national currency according to the ratio of adding 44%; those incurred after that date should all be repaid in national currency according to the ratio of adding 6%; (4) Continue to issue 10 million yuan of silver dollar legal tender to purchase silver from the public at the ratio of adding, with all of it allocated to the legal tender reserve fund. However, the above four points are merely the major outlines of the reform plan. As for the implementation steps and detailed methods, they still need to await considerable investigation and research before they can be determined. After the manuscript was completed and published in this journal, I also saw a newspaper report on Minister of Finance Kong's talk about reorganizing the currency system in Guangdong Province. To sum up, the content of his talk can be divided into four points: (1) The reorganization of the Guangdong currency should be based on the interests of all the people of Guangdong, and should not focus on the gains and losses of a few people, and it is even more necessary to strictly prevent the malpractices of excessive banknote issuance and improper transactions in the past. (2) The credit of Guangdong Province's subsidiary notes should be strengthened urgently, so it is necessary to first supplement the 7% shortfall in the cash reserve item and complete the guarantee reserve. (3) After the necessary procedures are completed, the Ministry of Finance will properly determine the exchange method and implement legal tender. (4) During the transition period, all receipts and payments are still allowed to use subsidiary notes as usual, but all tax revenues, if based on the central government's legal tender, should be converted into silver dollar legal tender at the market price of the day if legal tender is not available, but shall not exceed the calculation of adding 5%. Based on this, the central government has now set accurate steps for reorganizing the Guangdong currency. In the future, the establishment of the Central Bank, the issuance of silver dollar legal tender, the centralization of reserves, and the unification of foreign exchange are all technical issues in the reform and are not necessary to discuss. The biggest key to this is that there seems to be no decisive solution at present, which is the ratio of subsidiary notes to silver dollars. Now I would like to offer my personal humble opinion and reiterate the previous proposal for discussion.

(2) Author's Main Points

The previous article advocated that the ratio of subsidiary notes to national currency be set at adding 6%, and explained that by withdrawing subsidiary notes at this ratio, the people of Guangdong would only lose 10%, and the central government would also be able to handle it with ease, which is a win-win solution for reorganizing the currency system in Guangdong Province. However, some people may doubt my proposal, thinking that the ratio (the height of the ratio referred to in this article refers to the amount of water added when subsidiary notes are converted into silver dollars) is too high, which is tantamount to devaluing the currency value of Guangdong Province, and they are deeply afraid that this will affect prices and reduce the property of the people of Guangdong. In fact, my proposal is only the natural devaluation of subsidiary notes, not the devaluation of silver dollars. Now I would like to further clarify the impact on foreign trade, remittances from overseas Chinese, property income, and prices, finance, and industry, in order to clarify my point. However, there is still a prerequisite issue here: whether the central government will initially implement legal tender in Guangdong, allowing legal tender and subsidiary notes to circulate in the market at the same time, or stipulate that all receipts and payments should only be made with legal tender, while subsidiary notes can only be used to exchange legal tender. Although these two methods are only different in terms of gradual progress and rapid progress, they are essentially different paths. However, based on the current situation and considering local public opinion, it is appropriate to adopt a gradual approach. Now let us assume that a gradual approach is adopted, and after the implementation of the new currency system, legal tender and subsidiary notes are used together, and then explain the impact that will occur as follows:

(1) Foreign Trade After the implementation of the new currency system, the exchange rate will be stabilized, reducing the risks borne by merchants in foreign trade, as described in the previous article. As for the level of the ratio of subsidiary notes to national currency, it does not have much impact on import and export merchants. Because Guangdong Province's foreign trade, whether export or import, mostly goes through foreign commercial firms, using silver dollars or Hong Kong banknotes as the standard, which has little relationship with the level of foreign exchange. For importers who placed orders abroad before the reform and whose accounts have been settled before the goods are sold, the amount gained from the increase in selling price can compensate for the loss of currency devaluation, so there is no loss or gain. For those whose goods have not been sold and whose accounts have not been settled, although they will lose due to the currency devaluation when settling accounts, they will gain from the rise in prices when selling goods, so there is also no loss or gain. Those who place orders abroad after the reform will calculate the cost of selling goods using the new currency or converting it according to the new currency, so there is no loss or gain. Only those who placed orders before the reform and whose goods have been sold but whose payments have not been settled will inevitably suffer considerable losses; however, if they use the proceeds from the sale to purchase other goods in advance, the losses and gains will offset each other. (If payments are collected according to the legal tender implementation method described below, there will also be no loss or gain.) On the other hand, exporters who sold goods before the reform and whose goods have been shipped but whose payments have not been received will inevitably suffer losses because the price of goods has not risen but the currency value has fallen, but those who use Hong Kong dollars as the standard will also have no loss or gain. The same is true for those whose goods have not been shipped and whose payments have not been received, but who have already accepted orders. Those who accept orders after the reform can appropriately increase the price of goods even though the currency value is low, so there is also no gain or loss. In short, the level of the conversion rate (that is, the conversion rate between silver dollars and national currency, the same below) has no major impact on exporters and merchants; however, given the huge trade deficit in Guangdong Province in recent years, slightly devaluing the currency value to promote exports and suppress imports is also a good idea. However, if the currency value is excessively devalued, it will be greatly unfavorable to those who hold subsidiary notes. Therefore, weighing the two, the ratio of adding 6% seems to be quite appropriate. This is my first reason for semi-suppressing the value of subsidiary notes.

(2) Remittances from Overseas Chinese A large number of our Guangdong compatriots reside overseas. Over the decades, the amount of their hard-earned money remitted back to their motherland is considerable. According to Mr. Huang Yuanbin's estimate, the total amount of remittances from overseas Chinese in the 54 years since the Guangxu era has reached 6.2 billion yuan, a huge amount that is truly astonishing. Even during the recent period of economic downturn, the estimated amount remitted back each year is still more than 200 million yuan, of which Guangdong Province should account for at least half. This is truly a huge source of finance and industry for Guangdong Province. Our country's foreign trade has a trade deficit every year. The total trade deficit over the past few decades is about 7.5 billion yuan. Even in the recent three years, the average annual trade deficit is still as high as 50 million yuan. This huge loss in international balance of payments is mostly offset by the intangible income from remittances from overseas Chinese. The amount of remittances from overseas Chinese each year varies due to their own economic environment, and is also closely related to the level of exchange rates between countries. For example, during the global silver price crisis in 1920, overseas Chinese remitted hundreds of millions of yuan back to Guangdong. Conversely, in recent years of low silver prices, the amount of remittances has decreased relatively. Therefore, if the central government slightly devalues the value of subsidiary notes in this reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province, so that those who remit money back to Guangdong will receive considerable benefits in intangible ways, it will not only attract a large number of remittances from overseas Chinese in the short term, allowing Guangdong Province's finance to increase its activity, funds to be more abundant, and industries to develop, which will greatly benefit the economic recovery of Guangdong Province. This is the second reason why the value of subsidiary notes should be suppressed.

(3) Property Income A family's property and an individual's actual income do not increase or decrease due to changes in currency value, just as the amount of national wealth does not increase or decrease due to changes in the price of gold and silver. Gold and silver currency are only a measure of wealth value and a medium of exchange, and they lose their greatest utility outside of this. Paper money cannot be compared with the gold and silver it represents. Moreover, since the excessive issuance of subsidiary notes in Guangdong Province from November of last year to June of this year, it has lost its nature as a measure of value. Therefore, the value of subsidiary notes is low, and the value of property, except for the subsidiary notes themselves, can be said to be unchanged. The devaluation of subsidiary notes is originally a change in the ratio between subsidiary notes and national currency, not a change in the exchange ratio between Guangdong Province's property and property in other provinces and countries. Now let's use the example mentioned in the previous article to clarify it. For example, Shanghai produces goods A and Guangzhou produces goods B. The prices of goods A and B are both one yuan of national currency in Shanghai and 1.4 yuan of Guangdong currency in Guangzhou. After Guangdong Province's reform, anyone who has goods B can sell them in Shanghai and get one yuan of national currency, which is equivalent to 1.6 yuan of Guangdong currency. Therefore, merchants in Guangdong Province who have goods B or goods A will not have any changes in the value of their property due to the reform. Furthermore, from the perspective of foreign trade, for example, the price of Guangdong raw silk is 500 yuan of Guangdong currency per package, and the price of American wheat flour is 100 US dollars per package. At that time, the ratio of Guangdong currency to US dollars was 1 to 5 (Guangdong currency has never obtained a position in foreign exchange, and cannot actually be exchanged with the United States. This ratio is only converted from other currencies). Then exporting one package of raw silk can get 100 US dollars, and importing 10 packages of American wheat also requires 100 US dollars. That is, one package of raw silk can be exchanged for 10 packages of American wheat. After Guangdong Province's reform, assuming that the ratio of Guangdong currency to US dollars changes to 1 to 6, and the price of raw silk is not affected by the difference in supply and demand of the goods themselves, then its price should not change much, and it is still 100 US dollars. That is, exporting one package of raw silk can get 600 yuan of Guangdong currency, and importing 10 packages of wheat flour also requires 600 yuan of Guangdong currency. The exchange ratio of Guangdong silk and American wheat is still unchanged. From the perspective of the entire regional economy, the value of all property owned by the people of Guangdong Province does not increase or decrease due to the rise and fall of currency prices. Similarly, using this to disprove personal property income, after the reform, in addition to those who hold subsidiary notes and inevitably lose 10%, although the nominal income of the rest of the general public will decrease, the purchasing power of the national currency has obviously changed from before. Except for sporadic consumption that may be slightly more costly than before, the actual income remains unchanged. This can also be asserted.

(4) Prices The rise and fall of prices is actually a reflection of the rise and fall of currency value. If this reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province implements a 1% devaluation of the value of subsidiary notes, prices will naturally rise accordingly. However, because the exchange ratio between wood province and domestic and foreign goods has not changed, prices will return to normal after a certain period of time, which has been discussed in detail in the previous article. Moreover, since the implementation of the legal tender policy, subsidiary notes will inevitably be gradually absorbed through artificial and natural forces. Subsidiary notes themselves have lost their effectiveness as a measure of value, and can only be used as a medium of transaction, and even rise and fall independently from other prices, becoming a type of valuable securities, so how can they be enough to control the level of prices. As for after all the subsidiary notes are withdrawn, the silver dollars (referring to silver coins) will be fundamentally eliminated except as temporary subsidiary currency, and will no longer be an obstacle to currency unification. Therefore, although the ratio of adding 6% is set to withdraw subsidiary notes, it is actually not related to prices, that is, it is not related to people's lives. Within one or two months after the reform, if there is no standard for prices, then I think it is not difficult to remedy it. We can refer to the average price of Guangzhou in the six months before November last year, and convert it into national currency using the average ratio of silver dollars and national currency during those six months. We can also set a maximum limit based on the prices of major cities in the country in the recent period, and not allow prices on the market to be excessively raised. Soon, the use of the new currency in the province will be common, and trade with other provinces will be smooth, and then prices will inevitably return to normal.

(5) Finance According to investigations, the total annual revenue from national and local taxes in Guangdong Province is more than 50 million yuan. After prohibiting gambling and abolishing miscellaneous taxes, the annual revenue is 70 to 80 million yuan. Except for a small portion of which was originally based on silver dollars, the rest are received in silver dollars. During the transition period of this reform, those that are based on silver dollars will still be received and paid in subsidiary notes as usual; those that are based on silver dollars, if there is no silver dollar legal tender, will be allowed to be converted into silver dollars at the market price of the day; this method is originally to take care of reality and cater to public opinion, and is naturally appropriate. However, after the reform, in order to promote the implementation of legal tender, I think that the government should use national currency for all receipts and payments. Those that are based on national currency will naturally not be a problem. Those that are based on silver dollars should allow those who hold one yuan of national currency to pay taxes of 1.6 yuan in subsidiary notes within the period before the subsidiary notes are eliminated, in order to show fairness. Although the government will inevitably lose 10% in terms of tax revenue, this loss is very temporary. Once all the subsidiary notes are withdrawn (a period of one year or years can be set to withdraw all of them), the government will then consider the situation and set another conversion rate between silver dollars and national currency (this conversion rate is different from the conversion rate of subsidiary notes and can be set at around adding 44%) as the conversion standard. After the ratio is set, all amounts that are based on silver dollars, unless there is a contractual relationship previously set, can be converted into national currency, regardless of public or private receipts and payments. (Those with contractual relationships can be handled according to the legal tender implementation method described below.) In this way, the government's losses will be very temporary, and the losses will not be very large. Legal tender can also be promoted as a result. Moreover, the finances of Guangdong Province are fundamentally chaotic. During this transition period, the central government must provide subsidies. Although the government cannot but make some sacrifices, it can unify the currency system, stabilize finance, and increase tax revenue in the short term. This is also a good plan. On the other hand, if we only consider the current reduction in tax revenue and set a ratio of adding 5% or adding 3% to exchange subsidiary notes, it will not only put too much burden on the central government, but also will not be a blessing for the general public of Guangdong. Its disadvantages can be found in the opposite of the foreign trade and remittances from overseas Chinese described above. Some say that the ratio of national currency to Guangdong currency has been changed repeatedly, which may not be trusted by the people of Guangdong. They do not know that the ratio of adding 6% is only the ratio of exchanging subsidiary notes for legal tender, not the ratio of legal tender to silver dollars. Since the excessive issuance of subsidiary notes from November to June of this year, it has lost its position representing silver dollars. Although it can be used as a medium of transaction, it cannot be used as a criterion for measuring value. In the future, the government must not reduce its income to the extent of the depreciation of subsidiary notes due to short-term changes and the chaotic orders of the previous authorities (assuming that the central government does not maintain the subsidiary notes issued by Guangdong Province in the past, its depreciation may be as low as about 50%). The reason is very clear.

(6) Industry If this reform of the currency system in Guangdong Province is carried out smoothly, making the currency system unified, then prices in Guangdong Province will gradually stabilize, and foreign exchange will also tend to be stable. Investors will naturally be enthusiastic, financial activities will develop, and industry will inevitably become more developed. This has been discussed in the previous article. However, how the level of the conversion rate affects the industry must also be explained. According to the author's opinion, if the new currency system is implemented smoothly, making the price of subsidiary notes a type of valuable security other than currency, rising and falling independently from other prices, it will not have much impact on Guangdong Province's industry and commerce. However, in the one or two months after the implementation of the new currency system, the devaluation of subsidiary notes and the low exchange rate will naturally stimulate the development of industry and benefit the export of Guangdong Province's original industrial products. However, after a certain period of time, due to the unification of the currency system, domestic prices will tend to be stable, and this benefit will gradually disappear. At that time, the prosperity and decline of industry, in addition to the special reasons of the province, will naturally be transferred to the national economic policy. Some say that our country's production industry is still immature, and many emerging industries need to import foreign machinery and raw materials, and Guangdong Province is no exception. Therefore, if the conversion rate of this reform is too high, the production cost will also be high, and it cannot compete with imported goods. They do not know that if the ratio is high, although the price of foreign machinery is expensive, the price of imported goods will also rise at the same time. The way is not only can not hinder the export (because this kind of emerging industry, its products are expensive in the domestic market, but there is no change in foreign countries), and the other way can slightly suppress the dumping of foreign goods, it is beneficial and harmless. This is the third reason why the value of subsidiary notes should be suppressed.

To sum up, the ratio of adding 6% that Jin advocated has no impact on prices and property income; it is beneficial to foreign trade, remittances from overseas Chinese, capital activities, and industry; it can also find ways to avoid the loss of tax revenue in the future; and its greatest advantage lies in taking care of reality and facilitating the implementation of legal tender. The losses suffered by the people of Guangdong (only subsidiary note holders) are limited, and the government's burden is very light (please refer to the previous article). It is a win-win solution. On the other hand, if a ratio of adding 5% or adding 3% is set to exchange subsidiary notes, although the current tax revenue will not be reduced, the burden on the central government will be too heavy, the trade surplus will inevitably increase, remittances from overseas Chinese will be stagnant, capital will escape, credit will be tightened, and all kinds of disadvantages will emerge one after another. The harm is unspeakable.

(3) Legal Tender Implementation Methods

Based on my proposed plan, referring to the central government's intentions, and making slight revisions to the previous article, the following methods are proposed for the implementation of legal tender in Guangdong Province:

(1) According to the order to reform the currency system promulgated by the Ministry of Finance on November 3, 1935, the banknotes issued by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are designated as legal tender. The silver subsidiary notes (including municipal notes) issued by the two provincial and municipal banks in Guangdong Province, except for paying taxes, are still allowed to be used as usual for all receipts and payments, but only for a limited period of years.

(2) All government receipts and payments are limited to the central government's legal tender. People who pay taxes can use one yuan of legal tender to pay 1.6 yuan of silver dollars, but only for a period of years, and the ratio will be determined separately after the expiration.

(3) All silver shops, shops, and other public and private institutions or individuals who hold the above-mentioned silver notes are allowed to exchange the central government's legal tender at the ratio of 1.6 yuan of subsidiary notes for one yuan of central government's legal tender, and can go to the Guangdong Branch of the Central Bank to exchange legal tender without limit. After that, all receipts and payments, except for legal tender and subsidiary notes, shall not be made with foreign currency or cash; violators will be confiscated in full.

(4) Contracts established in the old unit of silver dollars (also known as Guangdong silver coins) or subsidiary notes (also known as Guangdong legal tender) should be converted into national currency according to the originally set amount, according to the ratio of silver dollars or subsidiary notes to national currency on the day the contract was established. On the due date, all payments shall be settled in the central government's legal tender. If the payment stipulated in the contract is calculated on a periodic basis, the conversion rate on the date the contract was originally established shall be used for settlement during the duration of the contract.

The above-mentioned conversion rate shall not exceed adding 6% or be less than adding 3%, which shall be investigated and verified by the Guangdong Provincial Department of Finance and announced separately. (Author's note: The announcement of this conversion rate can be from 1926 to the day before the implementation date of this law. If the price does not change much in a year or month, the average conversion rate of that year or month shall be used as the conversion rate for the whole year or whole month to avoid trouble. If the change is very large, the daily conversion rate shall be announced. As for those before 1926, a unified and uniform ratio can be used.)

The parties who established the contract can still settle payments in subsidiary notes if both parties agree.

(5) The order to reform the currency system promulgated by the Ministry of Finance on November 3, 1935 shall apply to all except as otherwise provided in this law.

(4) Explanation of Silver Two and Paper Six

The previous article advocated the second step of the reform plan, continuing to issue 30 million yuan of silver dollar legal tender to purchase silver from the public at the ratio of adding two; that is, one yuan of legal tender exchanges for 1.2 yuan of silver coins. However, it may be thought that the ratio of national currency to Guangdong currency set in my reform plan is sometimes adding six and sometimes adding two (referred to as silver two and paper six), which is inevitably contradictory. They do not know that the status of subsidiary notes cannot represent silver dollars, as mentioned above, and its price cannot be compared with cash silver. The reason is also clear. Today, when the system of managing currency is being implemented, the central government's legal tender has become inconvertible paper money. Therefore, the price of currency should not focus on the color of the currency or its cash reserves. The author has also considered this, but in today's China, where the credit economy is not yet fully developed, the psychology of the general public in society still focuses on the amount of cash reserves, which has a great relationship with the credit of the currency. The Ministry of Finance's declaration in June of this year also saw this, and it was a representation of consolidating the currency system and stabilizing finance. If the price of subsidiary notes in Guangdong Province is really determined by the amount of its reserves, then the actual price is only equal to about 43% of the original price, that is, one yuan of subsidiary notes is equal to 36 cents of legal tender (see the previous article); now it is converted at the ratio of adding six, that is, one yuan of subsidiary notes is equal to 63 cents of legal tender, which is 75% higher than the original price (the calculation formula has been seen in the previous article). It can be seen that the ratio of adding six is not entirely focused on the amount of its reserves, but is actually a way to comprehensively consider all aspects. As for one yuan of legal tender exchanging for 1.2 yuan of silver coins, the reason is nothing more than the two points mentioned in the previous article: one is to compare with the Shanghai market price, and the other is to make the degree of the price drop of silver coins and subsidiary notes mutually adapted. Now let's prove it with an arithmetic formula as follows:

Based on this, one yuan of subsidiary notes is only worth 75 cents of silver coins, that is, the price of subsidiary notes has fallen to 75% of the original price, not depreciated by 10%. They do not know that since Guangdong Province promulgated the order to centralize silver, 1.2 yuan of subsidiary notes have been used to purchase one yuan of silver coins. At that time, the price of subsidiary notes had already fallen to 10/12. Now, dividing 75 cents by 10/12, the result is still 90 cents.

That is, the price of subsidiary notes has actually only depreciated by 10%, which is no different from the result obtained from the two formulas calculated in the previous article. It can be seen that the ratio of silver two and paper six has a deep meaning in it.

(5) Conclusion

To sum up my reform plan, on the one hand, it is based on the two major principles of safeguarding the people's legal rights and reducing the government's burden; and on the other hand, it considers the impact on foreign trade, remittances from overseas Chinese, property income, and prices, industry, and finance, as the basis for decision-making. Finally, based on legal principles and taking into account local public opinion, the methods for implementing legal tender are determined. And its focus is especially on clarifying the status of Guangdong currency, explaining that subsidiary notes are not enough to represent silver dollars, and the ratio of adding six is only the ratio of exchanging subsidiary notes for legal tender, not the ratio of legal tender to silver dollars. It is advocated that a period of one year or two years should be set first to completely eliminate subsidiary notes, and then gradually abolish the silver dollar unit, which can not only avoid excessive burden on the central government, but also take into account the general welfare of the people of Guangdong. Although it is not a perfect solution, it is also a stable strategy. However, since this is a major reform plan, all implementation steps and practical methods must be carefully studied by the government and the people of the country. This article does not dwell on the issuance of new currency and the raising of public debt. However, with regard to the conversion rate, I think that the central government's decision to set the highest ratio at adding five, out of consideration for the suffering of the people of Guangdong, is already a special accommodation. If it is set at adding three or adding two and a half, the harm will be great, and I cannot agree. And my personal opinion is that the ratio should be determined separately according to the nature of Guangdong currency, with silver (referring to silver coins) adding two, silver dollars (the silver dollar mentioned here is not a kind of real object, it is used to represent the currency unit originally used in Guangdong Province, that is, the silver dollar standard referred to in Guangdong) adding 44, and subsidiary notes adding six, which is more appropriate.

— Written on August 27, 1936 at the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance —

Commercial News

Securities The Bond Market Was Extremely Stable Last Week, With Only Four or Five Horns of Difference Throughout the Week 177

Last week (August 24th to 29th), the Chinese Securities Exchange saw extremely stable market prices throughout the week. Although it was the last day of August, prices did not fluctuate much. The October market began, and although all issues were opened, there was not much difference. A riot occurred in Chengdu, but the market price of public bonds still changed little. Although the Guangxi situation remains unresolved, market prices also saw little fluctuation. The bullish trend is so firm for two reasons: commercial depression and abundant floating capital. Apart from a portion being used to evade foreign exchange controls, public bonds have become a relatively good investment for the middle class. According to some, seeing the bond market as easier to rise than fall, and with the closure of spot commodity investments, most have gone long. Therefore, unless there are major changes in the environment, the future market price will not change much. Looking back at last week, Monday was the last day for August futures. Although there was some squeeze, it was very limited, with market prices fluctuating between three and five. On Monday, only September forward months were traded, and trading was very sluggish, with market prices slightly better by two horns. On Wednesday, October futures started trading. A riot occurred in Chengdu, but due to the bullish firmness, the price only dropped by a small horn. Thursday was Confucius' birthday, and the market was closed. Friday was the delivery day for August futures, and the market was closed. On Saturday, there were rumors of clashes between the Guangxi army near Lingshan. At the same time, the situation in Sichuan remained unchanged. However, the market price only slightly dropped by one or two horns. The future trend is still being maintained. The week's market price ended with a mere three to five horns of difference. The total transaction volume was 23.16 million yuan. The results of the increases and decreases are compared in the table on the left (unit: yuan, transaction unit: hundred yuan).

Yarn and Cotton U.S. Cotton Saw New Low Prices, Industry Limited Purchases Resulted in Stable Closing, Indian Cotton Market Price Fell Sharply

Yesterday, when the U.S. cotton market opened, reports indicated rain in Oklahoma and northwestern Texas. News from Liverpool was unfavorable. Cotton farmers actively hedged, and Liverpool and New Orleans sold. Brokers liquidated their long positions, and prices for all months fell by three to five points. However, when the market price fell to a new low, industry limited purchases were very strong. Some Japanese firms also purchased, causing the market to stabilize. Before there is progress in the weather, buyers are hesitant to purchase, and the closing was stable. Spot prices fell by eight points, futures fell by five to eight points. British cotton spot prices fell by nine points, futures fell by five to eight points. Indian cotton retail investors sold, and market conditions were sluggish. The amount sold by futures traders was absorbed by cotton merchants through spread trading. The price of Pingor fell by 1.75 rupees, and Omra and White Raw Cotton fell by 2.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (dated 29th):

Pingor 153.25, down 1.75, 17.9

Omra 187.00, down 2.25, 33.30

White Raw Cotton 208.75, down 2.25, 37.50

According to a telegram from Bombay, the opening forecast for the 31st is: White Raw Cotton at 209 rupees, up 0.25 rupees; Omra at 188.5 rupees, the same as the previous day; Pingor at 153.5 rupees, up 0.25 rupees.

Spring and Autumn

Sixian Women's Tea-Picking Song 181

— Lei Lei

Small tea flowers bloom with five petals, three petals straight and two petals crooked. If you want straight, be straight to the end. If you want crooked, just be crooked, don't be straight and crooked.

The time has passed Ji Shi, and it's midday. Little Sister is delivering food across the field. I asked Little Sister what the dishes are. Sliced radishes and chopped green onions, a steamed egg in the middle.

Looking into the distance, Elder Sister is coming from that side, holding red embroidered shoes in her hand. I asked Elder Sister how much they cost? We only sell fresh flowers, not shoes, we keep the embroidered shoes as a signboard.

The green tea trees are short and can't be climbed. I lean on the tea trees and sigh. We pick tea all day long and fry tea all night long until the fifth watch. How can we have time for idle talk?

Drinking Tea 182

— Yin Feng

An English doctor advocates drinking a cup of mild, hot tea before breakfast every day, saying it has great benefits for both body and mind. He said: "A writer attributed his success to a cup of tea before breakfast. Many dieticians also approve of this habit because drinking a cup of mild tea before breakfast can not only stimulate the abdominal organs, but also make the mind clearer. However, people with weak stomachs or chronic indigestion should not have this habit, because they should absolutely not drink tea. If you put a set of alcohol stoves and a teapot on the table next to your bed, you can heat a cup of tea for yourself after getting up.

"Chinese tea is better than Indian tea because Chinese tea is not as strong as Indian tea. The tea we drink is best to be very mild and without milk. If you imitate the Russian style and add a thin slice of lemon to the tea, that's fine. Tea is not suitable for breakfast, and it is even more unsuitable to drink tea when eating meat at every meal. Meat and tea together are not good and are one of the main causes of indigestion. However, few people pay attention to this, and they are often seen drinking tea while eating rich dishes.

"Drinking a cup of tea in the afternoon is also very beneficial, but it should not be eaten with many meat sandwiches or pastries. The tea we drink should be hot, because tea contains tannin, which is an astringent acid that has the greatest effect when cold. There is no reason to drink tea before bed, because tea is a powerful stimulant. A person who drinks tea before going to bed is often awake and unable to fall asleep. Drinking a cup of hot water at this time can help digestion.

"Using tea as a mouthwash is the best thing to try. Natives in places like Ceylon and India where tea trees are planted not only drink a lot of tea, but also use cold tea leaves to clean their teeth. The acid contained in tea leaves can strengthen the gums and protect teeth.

Biluochun 183

— Zhu Shaofei

Biluochun, everyone knows it is a precious tea produced in Dongting East Mountain, which can be called famous at home and abroad. However, the output is not large, and when it is on the market, it is all bought by several so-called "outgoing households." They use it as a gift to give away, or relatives from afar entrust them to collect it on their behalf. The Biluochun sold in tea shops on the market, in the eyes of us Dongshan people, can be said that eight or nine out of ten are other types of tea disguised as Biluochun.

The preciousness of Biluochun is due to its curved shape, as thin as a needle tip, and with a layer of white fluff. When brewed, it is emerald green and fragrant. After drinking, it has a lingering taste, like tasting olives, first astringent and then sweet, sinking to the bottom of the cup, one bud and one leaf, each root just like picking it from the tree.

The method of making this tea is different from other places. It uses a pot for cooking rice. When making it, first heat the pot with a raging fire, and then "撲靑" (pu qing). (It is said that the Qian Zi should be heated as hot as possible when pu qing, the layer of white fluff on the tea leaves is entirely related to the temperature of the pot when pu qing.) Quickly move your hands up and down when placing the tea into the pot, when the tea leaves gradually show signs of moisture, the fire in the stove is temporarily stopped slowly. At this time, rub it with both palms, rub it into a ball and then scatter it, and continue until the pot temperature is low, then add firewood to the stove again. In this way, one pot must go through fifty to sixty times of rubbing and adding firewood. Only the methods of adding firewood and rubbing can successfully produce a few taels of Biluochun. In short, Dongting's Biluochun completely relies on slow, even fire and the technique of rubbing.

Unfortunately, our Dongshan tea trees are not planted in large quantities, they are only a by-product of the peasants. Some are wild in the mountains, and some use the empty land next to the orchards to plant a few trees. Except for the first batch of tea sold, the rest of the tea picked is kept for their own drinks.
