—

If you have reason, you can speak it, why bother clenching your fists

Village Teahouse 185

— Zhong Yue

People who have lived in the city for a long time can no longer imagine such a leisure place in the countryside - the teahouse.

As long as it is a slightly densely populated village, you can find a teahouse, two or even six or seven. These teahouses are narrow and the tables and chairs are old and dilapidated. The houses are probably two bays, the rear eaves of the first bay are higher so that sunlight can enter. It is connected to the first bay of the house and there is no patio in the middle. In the inner room of the first bay, there is a large coal stove. On the clean counter side by side, there are tea pots, tea cups and other sundries. Opposite the coal stove, there is a small tank for urination.

(Because tea drinkers drink as much tea as possible, there is also a considerable amount of urination) A dozen or so old square tables and long benches are placed in the outer room and the inner room, so the equipment of the village teahouse is complete.

Every day at seven or six o'clock in the morning, Lao Dian, who is also the tea house keeper, gets up busily, opens the door, pulls the coal stove, and smoke and coal ash suddenly fill the whole house, making people unable to breathe. Then the tea customers come slowly, find a seat with sleepy eyes, the tea house keeper wipes the tables and benches with a dark rag, and then makes tea. A basin and towel for spreading trachoma is attached. The tea customers wipe their faces very seriously and use the towel as a toothbrush. As soon as the tea is poured, you can see a lot of sediment. The cleanliness of the water and the quality of the tea leaves can be seen. Some tea customers bring their own teapots to the teahouse. Does he pay attention to hygiene? (Why doesn't he bring a tea cup?) No, because when he leaves, he can ask the waiter to pour a pot of boiling tea without extra charge and take it back for his wife and children to enjoy. More and more tea customers are coming, and the teahouse suddenly becomes active. The villagers' interest in playing mahjong is no less than that of people in the city. Although they are illiterate, they know all the numbers from one wan to ten wan, east, south, west, and north, without any error. The four sides of the table are surrounded by people watching. For a while, the sound of crackling and noise is endless. There are also several people sitting around a table, raising their voices and talking non-stop. This is what is called "eating jiang tea". Villagers have a temper. Whenever there is a dispute, they often go to the teahouse to judge. If they disagree, they put on a full martial arts performance, slapping the table, hitting the bench, throwing the pot and throwing the cup. The war will never stop without someone mediating. Therefore, the tables, benches, pots and cups in the teahouse are missing corners, lame feet, and dilapidated. This is the reason!

At noon, the tea customers all disperse in a rush.

The Story of Savings 186

— Qiu Lang

Saving is a virtue, which is generally recognized by the public, because no matter who, there will always be times when they encounter urgent needs. This is certainly not a problem for the wealthy, but in today's society, most people are economically disadvantaged, or make a living by working. Then, when they encounter urgent needs, they only have the method of borrowing from others, but whether they can borrow from others is uncertain. Only saving can solve this difficult problem. In the past, savings were made by taking silver or silver dollars, hiding them at home, or burying them underground, which was very dangerous or inconvenient. Now it is better, all banks have a savings department. Each person takes out a portion of their income and considers it as savings, and can send the money to the bank for deposit, but they must also deposit it in a reliable bank to avoid losses. Now I will write a short story about savings below to gain a smile.

In the past, there was someone named Jia, who was poor but liked to drink alcohol. He indulged in wine all day long. When he got money, he bought alcohol at the wine shop, and even if he had no money in his pocket, he would ask for credit from the wine shops. Therefore, every year during festivals, the wine bills from the wine shops were difficult to pay. Jia's wife repeatedly advised him not to listen and was extremely resentful. Later, she came up with a plan to limit Jia to only drink alcohol at home and to have her personally pay the money to buy it. Jia reluctantly agreed. From then on, every time Jia's wife went to buy alcohol, she would secretly take out some of the money and save it privately. Over time, small amounts accumulated into a large amount, but Jia did not know the mystery in this. At the end of the year, the wine shops came one after another to demand the old wine debts. Jia could not cope and was about to run away to avoid debts. Jia's wife said: There is savings money in the corner of the bed, quickly hand it over! As a result, after paying off the debt, there was still money left. Jia asked where the savings money came from? Jia's wife told him the reason, and he was deeply impressed by his wife's savings plan, which could relieve the pain of debt, and his affection for her increased a lot.

Although the above story is not very important, it can be known that the necessity of saving is something everyone should follow.

Changing the Nest for the Luan and Phoenix 187

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Jinxi Words Come Again, Drawing Emerald Leaves, Bridal Gown Surprises, Tears Wet the Crepe Gauze

Menglan was stunned, seeing her mother staring at her with such concentration, she suddenly smiled and said: Mom, what kind of person do you think I look like in this outfit? Madam Jiang didn't want to say that she looked like a bride, so she smiled and said: Why are you saying such silly things? No matter what clothes you wear, you are still you. Menglan shook her head and said: No, although a person's appearance will not change, if a person's clothes are very different from their usual appearance, then they will become a different person. Those who are detectives dress up as all kinds of people, farmers, merchants, and workers, just because they can change their appearance anytime and anywhere and turn into a different person. Madam Jiang said: How can you compare yourself to detectives? They know how to disguise. Menglan smiled and said: I don't care about any of these things, anyway, I feel like something in this outfit. It's very much like those mannequin models in the glass windows of Shanghai embroidery shops. As she spoke, she stood up straight, put her arms down vertically, held her face, and stood still for no less than two minutes. Madam Jiang didn't know what was going on at first, but after a while, she remembered and smiled: This, this child is naughty, take off the new clothes, don't get them dirty. Menglan twisted her body and smiled: Isn't it very much like it? Since you say so, I'll take them off. Madam Jiang sat on a chair by the window, looking at her daughter, feeling a little bored, and inadvertently pulled open the side drawer of the desk. There was still a key in the keyhole of the drawer. When Menglan saw it, she snatched it over, pushed the drawer in, and turned the key to lock it. Then she held the key in her hand, blushed, and said: Please, old lady, don't look at my drawer. Madam Jiang was stunned, looked at her and said: Why can't I look? A young lady, what else is there to hide from her mother? Menglan slowly took off her clothes, it took five minutes, and then replied, You can look at it if you want, but please don't be surprised after seeing it, it's very unlucky. As she spoke, she handed the key to Madam Jiang again, and then hid behind the lowered half of the curtain to change out of the red skirt she was wearing. Madam Jiang said: I know, there's nothing in your drawer, you're deliberately acting like this to make me angry, I'm too lazy to talk to you, the more I persuade you nicely, the more angry you get. After saying this, she automatically went out the door and downstairs. When Menglan saw her mother left, she sat alone in the tent, not moving at all, and took out an embroidered silk handkerchief from under the pillow. Because her hand touched the pillow, which aroused her thoughts of sleep, she fell on the pillow. Two hours later, Xiaolan came upstairs to invite her to go downstairs for lunch, but saw the lady's two feet sticking out from outside the tent, and she hadn't even taken off her shoes. A Glimpse of the Great Eastern Tea House 188

— Chen Liang

It is a vast, rectangular room with white walls, a white ceiling, and white light globes, giving a hazy, moonlit effect, but with long rows on either side. Four-leaf electric fans whirl overhead, mixing together the chattering and laughter of the patrons. Over a hundred small square tables are occupied by leisurely urbanites. There are office workers from foreign firms, land brokers, university students, young people who love literature and art, veteran writers, engineers, daughters of noble families and socialites, famous courtesans and dancers...

Emerald green curtains hang by the veranda. The tablecloths on the small square tables are beige, orange-yellow, and sky blue, and some are the same emerald green as the curtains—such soft hues.

This is distinctly different in style and taste from the old-fashioned "lou" (tower) or "yuan" (garden) tea houses. It is filled with the dynamism of all kinds of people. There is no need to meet certain qualifications or ask about status. Just have a leisurely heart, walk in, pick a table to sit down at, casually order a pot of black tea or oolong tea from a Southern waiter, accept the cold towel taken from the refrigerator, and casually wipe your nose or dry your hands.

Light a pipe, roll a cigarette, strike a match, read the newspaper's supplement, silently draft ideas, inquire about the latest market prices, discuss the merits of film actors, wait for close friends… each according to their needs. White-clad waiters do not pester with overly obsequious means like in other establishments. A cup of fragrant tea, a cigarette, a plate of dim sum, will make you forget the melting asphalt road outside, and the hurried people coming and going on the road...

Those carrying dim sum plates are all young girls wearing lake-blue long dresses, with healthy figures, white aprons, and long, flowing ribbons on their backs, making every patron feel lighthearted. And steamed buns, Tai Chi cakes, chicken siu mai... delivered from their fair and slender hands to your table, only five cents per serving, feels extremely cheap. In this way, even someone with indigestion will gradually increase their appetite. The shiny white fruit cart, coated with chrome, rolls smoothly from one corner to another on soft rubber wheels. Pears, purple grapes, Sunkist oranges... have fresh colors. A white porcelain dish and a small silver knife with an ivory handle are handed over by a girl with a head of black curly hair, or, if she personally peels a pear for you, you will realize that loneliness is not bitter!

Four Types of Tea Houses in Guangzhou 189

— Meng Chuanan

In the article "Tea Houses in Guangzhou" by She Li Jun published in this newspaper on the 18th, it is a pity that it was not detailed enough and also deviated slightly from the facts. Now, according to what I know, I will write it haphazardly, continuing the unfinished work like a dog's tail. Please don't ridicule me.

Cantonese people are addicted to tea. They feel uncomfortable if they don't visit a tea house every day. Therefore, tea houses have sprung up in response to the times, as numerous as carps crossing the river. No matter the main street or small alley, there must be three or four dotting the landscape. Their types can be divided into four: "tea houses," "tea rooms," "tea kiosks," and "tea sheds."

Tea houses are located in bustling main roads, with magnificent architecture, splendid decorations, exquisite tea sets, delicious dim sum, and slightly higher tea prices. Occasionally, famous female singers from Guangzhou and Hong Kong are invited to sing in rotation (such as Yue Er, Ben Yue, Hua Niang, etc. all came from these places and became famous as a result). A song sung with a clear voice entertains the guests. Front row seats cost from five jiao to one yuan per cup. Those without sufficient financial means dare not try it. The most famous tea houses are "Taoran" at Xihaokou, "Huirian" on Huiai Road, "Yuexiu" on Yuexiu Road, "Hongmian" outside Xiaobeimen, and "Yijing Erda Sanyuan" on Changdi, etc.

Tea rooms mostly rent upper floors to start their businesses, with elegant and clean decorations and fewer seats. Tea prices are divided into five-fen and one-jiao types. The buns and snacks made are exquisite and palatable, and the tea servants' service is also attentive. The most famous tea rooms are "Park Tea Room" in front of the park and "Mayflower" on Huiai East Road, etc. Most of the tea drinkers are from academic circles.

Tea kiosks are located on small roads, with small scope and simple decorations, and the tea prices are very cheap, only two fen, two fen eight, or two fen four per cup. Dim sum such as barbecued pork buns, shrimp dumplings, siu mai, fun guo, and Malay cake, etc. are only two fen per plate with two pieces. Most economical people go there. "Youzhan Tea Kiosk" on Zhonghua North Road and "Deyi Tea Kiosk" in front of the Central Memorial Hall are the outstanding ones among them.

Tea sheds are mostly set up in poor mountain villages and remote areas, built by the stream, with thatched roofs. A table and a few stools have a special charm. They mostly use spring water to brew tea. The spring water is sweet and refreshing, so the tea is fragrant, which is certainly not comparable to the city. Therefore, those who have lived in the city for a long time turn their eyes and mostly go to tea sheds to drink tea and talk. On holidays, they open a room to play mahjong. "Da Bao Han" and "Xiao Bao Han" outside Xiaobeimen on Baohan Road, etc., are bustling with activity and business is thriving.

"On the tea house, vendors are busily shuttling to sell various snacks." This is actually She Li Jun's misunderstanding. Those who come and go to deliver dim sum are not vendors. They are tea servants hired by the tea owner (tea masters) who are in charge of serving the guests. Dim sum is not sold by the tea servants themselves. The entire business is entirely operated by the tea owner. Dim sum is two pieces per plate (only chicken meat buns and century egg pastries are one piece). According to Guangzhou tea rules, dim sum can be returned. Those that have not been eaten are not counted; while Shanghai tea houses such as "Taotao" and "Xinya" calculate the original plate and cannot be returned. This is something that tea drinkers from other provinces must know.

A Discussion

Japan's Concern for China's Revival 200

— I

The Pacific Society held its sixth conference the other day. First, Dr. Hu Shi, the Chinese representative, gave a speech, stating that any Chinese government that is strong enough to unify the country and enhance the country's position will not be tolerated by Japan. This has almost become national policy in Japan. The Japanese representative stood up immediately to object and stated that he would answer point by point tomorrow. I think that under the current brutal situation of Japan in Guanwai and North China, it is difficult to justify that Japan does not oppose China's unification. Therefore, they had to declare in advance that they would answer point by point tomorrow, which is the same as the storytellers who sell off suspense, "Please come early tomorrow."

After a night of deep thought and deliberation, I think Mr. Yoshizawa must have made a magnificent speech. Sure enough, this magnificent speech was published in the newspaper the other day. The important points of his reply are about three points: (1) China and Japan are of the same race and culture, and are very concerned about China's revival, (2) Japan does not oppose China's unification, and (3) Japan opposes China's unification because China itself is not good.

For the first point, because China and Japan are close at hand and of the same culture and race, we are indeed grateful for Japan's concern and have benefited a lot. Not counting the past, the September 18 Incident was Japan's concern, the January 28 Incident was Japan's concern, accommodating ordinary Chinese traitors and ruffians to disrupt the political situation in North China was Japan's concern, and the "free trade" everywhere, I don't say smuggling, was Japan's concern. The construction of airfields by force and the unlimited increase of troops are all Japan's concern.

For the second point, he said that he does not oppose China's unification. What is the evidence? Well, he said that a few months ago, Chen Jitang of Guangdong failed and stepped down, and Guangdong and Nanjing reunited. From this point of view, Japan has never hindered China's unification. In fact, Chen Jitang's failure and stepping down were due to the Guangdong army's own realization that they were unwilling to use the same room's weapons and be exploited by the fisherman. This is something Japan could not help but really loathed to forget. Therefore, Chen Jitang's stepping down has nothing to do with Japan and is not enough to prove that Japan does not oppose China's unification. This is really the so-called scratching an itch through boots.

The third point is that China has repeatedly increased tariffs, violated treaty obligations to Japan, and especially disregarded the 1905 Protocol and built a parallel line to the South Manchuria Railway in Manchuria. This statement is the basis for opposing China's unification and undermining China's unification. In short, raising tariffs and reducing tariffs are the absolute freedom of independent countries and are not restricted by any country. Moreover, raising tariffs is not only aimed at Japan alone. If the tariffs of one country are raised, and all other countries are exceptions, why don't other countries come out to oppose it, but Japan uses this as an excuse to kill people? As for building a parallel line to the South Manchuria Railway, it is also absolute freedom to build China's railways on China's land. I really don't understand why this offends Japan so deeply.

Mr. Yoshizawa also said that recalling the Washington Conference, the Nine-Power Treaty was signed to guarantee China's territorial integrity, and Japan initiated it. Whether this matter was initiated by Japan remains to be verified. Even if Japan initiated it, it is not known whether Japan has any other intentions. However, this matter should be thanked, but may I ask what country destroyed the various events that damaged China's territorial integrity after September 18? What country tore up the League of Nations? I am afraid that Mr. Yoshizawa, even with a hundred mouths, cannot explain it. Chinese compatriots are being deported back to China batch after batch, but they say that overseas Chinese in Japan are treated with courtesy everywhere. The pseudo-Manchu signboard is hung high in the eastern provinces, but they say that they are very concerned about China's revival. Alas, what is this?

However, Mr. Yoshizawa still has a trace of conscience, and said that we will deeply know that our actions against China are not without improprieties. Then, Mr. Yoshizawa is already aware of this. Why do you say that if the two countries want to restore proper feelings, it is best for China to change its attitude and cooperate with Japan? This statement is exactly the opposite. Assuming that the two countries want to restore proper feelings, Japan should change its attitude first and cooperate with China before there is room to restore proper feelings between the two countries. Otherwise, it will be a day that is unbearable to look back on.

Flowers 202

— Yun

I have wanted to write an article about flowers for a long time, but I have not written a single word after picking up the pen several times. Because I love flowers passionately, there were dozens of pots of flowers I planted by hand in the yard of my hometown. After I left my hometown, they all withered. When I think of writing an article about flowers, I immediately remember the unbearable death of those dozens of flowers, and finally I put down the pen.

After coming to Shanghai, naturally there is no opportunity to plant flowers, and the environment does not allow you to do so. As a second choice, I wanted to buy a few flowers to offer on the desk, but it seems not very possible; although those flower shops display various seasonal flowers every day, the price is really too expensive. I am almost like a tramp standing outside the glass window of a bakery, and I have to stand outside the door of an attached flower shop for a while every day. Those flowers are really too lovely.

The shop owner is a Western woman, so most of her customers are Westerners. There are especially many people buying flowers on Saturday afternoons and Sunday mornings, but those are not people who love flowers. They are betting their love with their girlfriends with flowers. So the price is too expensive. That is also one of the reasons.

Page 18

On Nanjing Road, there are many little girls who specialize in selling white orchid flowers, and naturally there are also old women. Their patrons are mostly female customers. They like to stand outside department stores or silk shops, and when they see female customers coming out with goods, they always follow them closely, hoping to sell a flower or a flower ball, but those little girls are often disappointed, because those ladies have "monthly" flower sellers who deliver them to their houses every morning on a daily basis. If it is in the evening, then it is time for female customers to buy flowers, because the female customers who pass by there in the evening are said to be mostly from the game field; as for why those who go to the game field must buy a flower or a flower ball to decorate their lapels, that is a side effect of flowers, which is inconvenient to say more about.

Speaking of this, do those little girls only do business in the evening one day? It is definitely not the case. There are some people who spend a few copper coins and flirt with them, or even pinch their arms and grab their palms, and throw the flowers they bought on the road in the blink of an eye. That is simply a waste of natural resources, but it is also a kind of side effect of flowers.

I once went to Nanyang Bridge with a friend before dawn to visit the flower market. Outside the iron gate, the sidewalk and the center of the street that lead directly to the newly opened Heping Road are all flower sellers who come to the market. The flower market is centered on the Wanhualou Tea House. Everyone brews a pot of tea and waits for patrons there. Those little girls who sell white orchid flowers walk back and forth there at this time, stringing the flowers with lead wire. As for the situation of flirting and touching here and there during the sale, it is even worse than on Nanjing Road. The old women pouted and mumbled that they could not get good flowers and that business would be discounted, but that kind of vile insult could be avoided. If she had also been a flower-selling girl since she was a child, then she would have to grieve that her age was running too fast; not being able to get good flowers when buying flowers, and no one talking to her when selling flowers, this is exactly a symbol of the fate of flowers! Today, they are attached to the lapel and inserted into the vase, and tomorrow they will all be thrown into the trash can.

I was really happy that day. I bought a bunch of my favorite dahlias. Because dahlia is the name of one of my girlfriends, it is a pity that I failed in the love bet. I don’t know whose vase that bright dahlia is inserted into now? I hope she will always be eye-catching and lovely, and not wither like the dozens of flowers in my hometown.

Now I have an artificial flower inserted in the bottle on my desk, which I bought from a department store, and the flower is naturally a dahlia. Although it has been too long, the petals are full of dust, and the red color is about to turn dark yellow. However, because of my love for it, even if it turns from dark yellow to ocher, it is still a lovely dahlia; moreover, I have bought expensive flowers, and if I abandon her, that empty bottle will also lose its effect.

I have already written a lot, and I will leave the unfinished part to write when I have the opportunity.

The autumn scenery is fading, and winter has arrived. Crows crow in groups in the cold wind. Vermilion spits out sunshine. The moonlight is faint, and the night fog is thick. The beauty sits alone, lost in thought. Facing the lonely lamp, she doesn't realize that her chest is stained with tears. Unfortunately, her uncle and mother died one after another. She is lonely and has few younger brothers. Drifting aimlessly, she is寄 in another village. She has spent several winters in misery. But she was promised marriage by her aunt.

Saying that the gentleman is a romantic and noble official. Since the year of the candlelight wedding. Who knows that the first wife has a different temper. She is ignorant, unknowing, and unkind. How can they have a happy heart with zithers singing in harmony. There has never been a single word of intimacy. The couple seems to have met strangers. I hate that he often goes to the brothels and spends the night. I hate that his strange habits are different from others. It is hateful that the old man under the moon has no discernment. It is a great pity to have the wrong red thread. I believe a sentence of the ancients. Beautiful women have a thin life since ancient times. Several times I think of things that are depressing. I will be lonely in my boudoir for the rest of my life. It is pitiful that I am the daughter of the former rich family. How can I learn to be the same as civilized women. The only thing to dispel is the music. The jade flute is hard to blow with thousands of heavy sorrow. How sad is the splendor years, lonely sleeping. Half of the brocade quilt, half of the bed is empty. I feel a little tired and fall into a dream. But I was called by the magpies under the eaves calling in the west wind. I am infinitely desolate, suing the sky.

Leftover Music

The upper and lower volumes of the radio teaching Chinese and Western books published by the Art Lecture Hall have been taught in Yuanchang Leitai and Li Shude Radio Station since September. The time is Tuesday and Thursday mornings from 6:00 to 6:30, and Sunday mornings from 7:00 to 8:30. Those who want to purchase lecture notes, please contact the above two radio stations. In addition, in order to examine the performance of various listeners and conduct public exhibitions, the club specifically solicits paintings, (no matter what is painted with (please send them directly to Li Shude Radio Station on Baike Road or Yuanchang Radio Station on Caishi Road so that the first radio transmission painting exhibition can be held on a regular basis. The degree and age are not limited.

The Shanghai Bazilu Songbai News Agency concert has been thriving since its restoration. In order to expand its scope, the original club address is narrow and insufficient for application. It was relocated to the third floor of 1312 Bazilu intersection of North Sichuan Road on the 25th of this month. All walks of life are welcome to discuss and guide at any time, and new members are solicited. Recently, it has been heard that those who join the club to study music are very enthusiastic.

In order to make all walks of life understand the difference between so-called radio dramas and dramas, Liu Yawei specifically wrote and printed 1,000 copies of the "Our Self-Analysis" special edition. Those who attach three copies of postage and send them directly to Liu at Chongde 19, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, can also get a copy of the "Shanghai Beach Half-Monthly" magazine edited by Liu.

Movie

Please See the Plot of Xilimen 208

"Comedy writer" Huang Jiamo's other new work after "Incarnation Girl", "Xilimen", is now being filmed by Yihua Company, directed by Yue Feng. The script is Huang's proud work last year, which was highly praised by the producer (editor's note: that is, Yihua). Director Yue Feng and all the actors were very excited when working. The film has great and magnificent scenes, novel and compact plots, and is full of fun. It is unprecedented. It is not only a realistic portrayal of Chinese folk customs, but also a vivid form of typical rural figures. Everyone who has read the script of the film can't help but laugh and applaud. Director Yue Feng's technique is particularly bright and brisk, lively and interesting. The plot of the film is listed below to see a glimpse:

Village girl's beauty, playboy's admiration.

Marriage proposal competition, matchmakers compete.

Family education is wrong, the father indulges the son.

Beside the festival and filial piety archway, the widow is flirtatious.

Stopping the sedan chair to snatch the bride, getting rid of the golden cicada.

Fat pigs accompany the dowry, and daughters are in the same car.

Secretly crossing Chencang, please enter the urn.

The sins are deep, and He Yan shows filial piety.

Poem for – Bai Yu Shuang in the Red Crabapple Blossoms 209

On the stage –

Audiences are captivated, adore, and go crazy for your talent and beauty!

But who knows how miserable your real life is?

You cannot refuse the powerful figures offering wine and passing cups,

And your good-for-nothing husband constantly subjects you to fists and kicks,

Because you cannot satisfy his exploitative desires!

And the burdens of the family are added to your shoulders,

You don't resist,

You are also powerless to resist,

Because the forces of feudalism are surging high,

Oh, you weak woman;

Your whole life is buried under these feudal shackles!

Bearing tears of pain,

Drinking the bitter wine of life,

But you are also filled with bright hope,

Entrusting your life to your son,

However, your hope is soon extinguished,

Fate has carved another deep wound in your heart,

"Oh! It's over, my son is over, I'm over, everything is over,"

You are as grieved as if you have gone mad,

But the gluttonous kiss of the violent man is still not satisfied,

And sends his henchmen to force you to the military governor's mansion,

You are determined to die,

The banquet is filled with such tragic laughter and scolding,

And you even draw out a white blade to stab the violent man in the chest,

But you are, after all, a weak animal,

And are soon imprisoned in a high wall where the sun never shines,

Although you finally regained your freedom later,

You are already homeless,

Wandering in the vast sea of people,

Traveling a long and arduous journey,

Until you encounter your son whom you haven't seen for ten years,

A hint of a smile finally unfolds on your melancholic face!

Tan Ying and Cheng Bugao's collaborative performance of the scene "Xiao Ling Zi"

New Information from the Star Grand Theater 210

The Star Grand Theater on Qingdao Road was originally founded by an American company. Recently, after being operated by the Chinese-owned Youyi Co., Ltd., the interior has been renovated, replacing it with the world's first-class Western Electric sound system and transmission rubber. The perfection of the screen equipment is especially outstanding among Chinese-owned theaters. The grand opening is scheduled for September 3rd. The first excellent film of the new autumn season is the detective blockbuster "Yu Gangzuan" produced by the Star Film Company. Following screenings are already scheduled for great new films such as "New Marriage Massacre," "Peach Garden Dream," and "Rebirth." The lineup is so splendid that nothing can compare.

New Publication Introduction

The six-volume, third issue of the Star Bi-Monthly has been published. Starting with this issue, the number of pages has increased by four, and the content is exceptionally rich and sophisticated. This issue includes articles such as Mo Ming's "On the Themes and Production of National Defense Films," Xia Boyang's "How I Played 'Que Pai Ye Fu'," Mu Weifang's "Is a Union Necessary Between Filmmakers and Film Critics?" Lu Si's "Please, Writers, Step Out of the Ivory Tower," and Bo Lang's "A Few Words on Children's Film Week." Other features include the film commentary "Bi-Monthly Chat," "World Film Scene," etc. In addition to the original bi-monthly cartoons, there are also沫旦's works "No Smuggling Allowed," "Children's Film Week," and "I'll Take Your Picture," etc.; photos include Chen Boer, "Xiao Lingzi," "United in Life and Death," "Eternal Smile," "Red Crabapple Blossoms," etc. In addition, there are several Soviet children's films and Gorky's "Mother" paintings, among other detailed items that cannot all be listed. The price remains at six cents.

The Qianqiu Publishing House, located at No. 4, Lane 153, Carter Road, Shanghai, publishes "Yuan Meiyun's Biography," which details her life's secrets and scandals. The photos are many, and they are rare sensual shots from the outside world. Each volume is sold for only one dime of national currency, and stamps are accepted.

The semi-monthly magazine "Streamline" will be launched soon. The content includes domestic and foreign current events, commentary, special features with celebrity interviews, sketches of society and rural areas, as well as anecdotes and reviews of film, dance, sports, and all other dramatists; photos include current events, beautiful women, sports figures, and star photos of beautiful dance, etc.; cartoons: woodcuts, etc. It is edited by Mr. Gan Nailiang and published by Xiaoyao Publishing House.
